Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "contusing cure," and it is that you make the patient who has this illness shave the hair that he has on his forehead, then make three incisions on his forehead equally along the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the incisions be like two fingers wide in the middle of the forehead going down to the nose, and the other two at the two temples above the eyelids, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are at the two sides above the eyelids;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and keep your hand away from the joining of the two jaws, and let each wound be the size of three fingers across joined;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths to wipe away the blood, then put the sharp spatula on two sides of which this is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision that is near the temple to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape all the skin that is between the two incisions to the whole surface that is on the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second, and then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	then put into the first incision the instrument which is called a "cultellary", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is smooth, not sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting side towards the flesh next to the skin, and the smooth side towards the bone, and put it in until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to that which appears of the skin, and then similarly do in the middle incision to the other opening;
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then draw out the blood equally, and press the place for the blood taken;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put in each incision a tent of old cotton, and put on cloths moistened in wine and oil and vinegar, and guard against hot abscesses coming there;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day untie the ligature, and apply a great quantity of warm water there, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments with which one treats wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When to some comes sharp catarrh customarily, and you see the eyes swollen and small, and weakening of the sight, and the eyelids burned;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and in the head there is sharp pain, and the patient sneezes;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then know by these symptoms that those matters and that catarrh do not come forth except from many veins, and the best cure that there is, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to shave his forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another a little wider.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then separate the two lips of the incision and put old cotton and linen tents there;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then bind over it cloths moistened in wine and oil, and beware of a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow there, then treat it with drying things that cause flesh to grow.
En teil maniere:	In this manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster from them;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and apply it to these wounds to cause flesh to grow throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping up of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that falls into the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	either grains, or an animal, or a mine stone or something similar like iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seeds, such as lentils, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing things such as water and vinegar and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or other kind of thing falls into the ear that does not adhere to the ear, nor grow in the ear, put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, instill a little violet oil or oil of sweet basil, then administer extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make him sneeze with sneezing powders, and stuff his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and stretch the ear upward.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Often it comes out by this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come out, administer extraction with fine forceps, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it jumps out with the forceps, it is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, administer extraction with a fine probe of small diameter;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not come out by this, make a chain of bronze and place the head of the chain in the hole of the ear firmly, and plug that which is around the chain with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the chain;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then pull it out forcefully, for many times it comes out as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out in this manner, take birdlime, and place on it some instrument which is sharp for this purpose, and place a bit of cotton around it;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not come out by all these things that we have said, hasten to cut open the ear before a warm abscess and spasm come;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of the incision is that you first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and draw out blood according to the measure of his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear in the fatty tissue or the dependent part;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the incision be like a crescent moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and suck it out quickly with your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, administer a thin spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract it with fine tweezers and a suction device, as we have said, so that the extraction is easier.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water then that falls into the ear, it is necessary that the patient first use sneezing powders, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out because of this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If not, take many stones according to the length of your little finger, and light, and warm them a little in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and let the patient put one in the opening of his ear, and jump on it with his feet from the other side, and strike with another stone on the stone which is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not cease doing this, stone by stone, until all the water comes out, and thus it will all jump out;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and take the other end with fire until the greater part of the reed is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then do likewise with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small, like a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is large enough to be felt, then use extraction with tweezers;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and that is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of the worms that infest the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help, then you must look into the ear in the sun:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if any worms appear, then remove them with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, then take the candle of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And put the finest end into the ear according to the amount the patient can tolerate, then suck strongly on the whole candle;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey in coming out, then wrap cotton around the candle as I have said for the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not jump out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in killing worms, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and distill your oils and your medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which here is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And let it be of silver or bronze, narrow below with one small hole, and open above for distilling;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press the distillation inside with a well-made bronze instrument for this purpose, and if you wish take a rasp and wrap cotton neatly around the point;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour your oil or your juice, and what you wish of your medicines into the funnel, and the funnel should be in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then put inside the rasp with all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or completely in the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient feels it inside, and let the distillation be a little warmed by the fire, before it is distilled into the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping up of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	Some children are born who have no opening in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to adults by the stopping up of a wound, or of flesh grown inside the ear, and this stopping up sometimes comes deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes the opening is slightly obstructed, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which comes deep, so that one cannot see it, is of difficult healing in many conditions, and in that which one sees it is necessary that you put the ear of the patient in the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside;
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the obstruction clearly, then work with all this spatula of which here is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind, entirely smooth, so that it does not wound the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the obstruction is of raw flesh or of the body of the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers, and cut it lightly, until that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is deep within the ear, then take a thin, light rasp and heat it a little in the fire, then place it in the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the obstruction from which the patient feels pain in hearing, pierce lightly, and take care that you do not injure the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then place in the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and moisten it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle on powdered vitriol;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear swollen, then you must remove the tent and use another tent moistened in a cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloths in cold water, and apply it to the ear, and use other treatments that stop bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the papillary muscles
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This athelu, which comes in the papillary muscles of the eyes when they are moist and dry, requires that you stretch them with forceps and pincers, and cut it with a spatula from its roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put crushed vitriol on the place.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if blood flows, cauterize it with a fine lenticular cautery, and the cauterization after the incision is better;
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and often they return, when something remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Often there appear in the eyelids things that resemble hail in their form and hardness, and because of this this illness is called "hail", and is a gathering of moisture, thick in the eyelid above and below;
li ovraiges est telz:	the procedure is as follows:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	observe whether the hail moves from one side to the other, and this is easy to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	then make an incision wide, then lightly scrape each part, then grasp it with forceps, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	if you cannot cut it without piercing the eyelid a little, it harms the patient nothing;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the fissure is large, then close it with a suture, and treat it until it is healed;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not use force, for ointments restore it immediately and generate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the hailstone descends into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, invert the eyelid, and extract the hailstone with forceps, and cut and press on one side and the other;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the eyelid is separated by the incision, that harms nothing;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the hailstone is removed, bathe the eye with salt water, and treat the area with something that generates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease which is generated in the webs of the upper eyelids, and this happens more to children than to any other people, and it greatly harms their eyes, and they get cataracts in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because tears rush to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and because of this they always lie on their faces, and sleep thus, and their eyelids are moist under their eyebrows because the swelling and the appearance have covered the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head in your lap;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains the exinach of each part, then put it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered in the middle of the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then cut in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit of the width, and let it not be larger than the wound that one makes to open a vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and cut the skin deeply until you reach the exinach;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in several instances exinach comes from the slit, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Then extract it all in one piece with a piece of lint between your fingers, from the outside, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is separated;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and be careful not to insert into the slit, that you do not bring the whole spatula down to the eye, that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the slit, slightly enlarge the slit a little until it appears;
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and apply them to the area, and bind tightly with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are some men who grind salt and apply it to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess appears in the area, treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the testicles
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs grow in the testicles in addition to the natural ones, and they are left to grow, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as habitual tears and softening of the testicles and albuginea, so much so that this is the cause of the destruction of the eyes;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and the cure is according to four methods:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	either by cautery with fire, or by a sharp medicine according to what is described in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suture or by cautery, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you place the patient's head on your lap, then turn the testicle towards your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is turned, that is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then put a needle with thread on it;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let this be near the edge of the testicle where the hairs grow near those hairs, and pull the thread above with the testicle, and turn it back;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then cut in the part below the testicle, below the adjacent hairs, with the sharp spatula, from the large tear to the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then pull out the thread, and place under the testicle a small tent of cotton and cloth, then mark on the testicle a figure of a wedge, like a myrtle leaf, and however it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you wish to raise the testicle which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if there is someone who needs to cut a large quantity of the testicle according to how the testicle is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then cut with the spatula on the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large tear to the small one;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the hook in one of the two angles of the heart, then peel it all;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then join the two lips with a stitch of a needle with a fine wool thread, and wipe away the blood, and cut off the superfluity of the threads above the two eyebrows with some sticky substance, if you wish to do so;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, do not worry about it, then leave the suture and the threads for three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then treat the wound without suture with drying and constricting things, for the skin retracts at the bottom of the wound and its joining, but the suture is better (as the ancients said), and it is work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and there is another method:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you mark the skin with a shape that is like a myrtle leaf, as we have described, at three inches apart according to the shape that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is above with small, equal forces according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you are not able to hold the forceps, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with one thread, and put it in the middle of the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and put one other thread near the large tear, and the second thread near the small one, and bring together the threads evenly between your fingers;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have described, then bring together the two lips of the wound by suture, and treat it until it is healed;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointment;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the wound are inverted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	then you must use what we have said about the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the suture in one and the other is more skillful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of cankers is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you invert the wound and cut into it according to what I have said, and then make two cankers by art, and two fine ligatures as long as the wound and the width of the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut at the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then carefully join one and the other over what remains of the wound's edge, and tightly pull the two cankers of the two parts;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which is constricted will die and wither and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it is slow, then cut it with force, then treat it until it is healed;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is closed, and the skin is lifted, and the hairs will no longer prick;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the shape of the two cankers that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The procedure is such that you take a fine needle, and thread it with a soft and fine silk thread;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then bring the ends together and tie them subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then arrange in the chase another fine silk thread briefly, and tie the ends of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then let the patient put his head in your lap;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be near the sun so that the work is clear, for it is a subtle and delicate work, then put the needle with the chase at the root of the added hair, and make it pierce the skin quickly until you pull it above the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then pull the hair up to the chase, and put that hair into the chase, if there is one or two or three or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then withdraw your hand until the hairs come out with the chase through the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the chase is pulled and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the chase downwards with all the thread that you have arranged there, until the chase comes out of the hole above and you see it with the vision of your eye;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	then pull out the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair heals in its place and the flesh grows over it;
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hair is small, accompany it with a long hair from the natural hair, and let it grow with that one, or leave it, until it is lengthened and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or corruption comes to the eye, there are two kinds:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or a cut, or a cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of working on it is that you split that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put linen tents inside, and bind it until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not necessary that you use in the treatment of it things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do that, the illness returns worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but work with softening things, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and rose water or mallow and linseed, boiled, and diachylon ointment melted in some oil, and wrap a tent in it, and cure it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the key to your treatment is that you ensure that it does not heal according to the way it was before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these treatments that we have mentioned are nothing but remedies for this illness, so that it does not return as it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that grows in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is below, which is truly called "axacrati," and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accidental [occurrence] comes from a wound and a fissure and a cautery and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the method of treatment is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and stick it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out at two ends of the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then stretch the flesh upwards with the needle, and cut it with a spatula one finger wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the pupil returns as it should, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, take a rasp and put it in the fissure, and turn the pupil, and make two incisions on the inside of the pupil;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the ends of the two incisions be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make an angle so that when they are joined, the shape is like the shape of a letter called "I Greek";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then remove that flesh, according to the amount that its sides are sharp underneath, of that which surrounds the pupil, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a wool thread;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with what we have said of softening medicines, and with tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a fissure or suture or cautery, then you must make a full incision under the hairs of the eyelids, and according to what is above;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate between the two lips with a tent, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares a remedy with all his power so that he may restore the form to its natural shape;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what is needed in work and instruments in various situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sudden swelling of the eyelid
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this adhesion happens to many men in such a way that the eyelid above is adhered to the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must place the point of a razor under the eyelid and lift it up;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and stretch it with pincers, until you cut what is adhered with a thin spatula, which is neither too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient cannot suffer that the too sharp spatula injure the eye;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and let your incision, with which you scrape away that adhesion, be light, so that the eyelid returns to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and when that adhesion is healed, they sometimes apply salty water to the eye, and wash it with fresh water, and with eyewash;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then place between the eyelid and the eye a linen tent, and place on the eye wool moistened in egg white;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day use eyewash and soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that a nail is according to two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	it is nervous and similar to hard tissue, and another which is not nervous, but is similar to congealed white moisture, so that when one touches it with iron and thinks to grasp it with pincers, one cannot;
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both forms begin towards the larger tear duct, and grow little by little until it covers all vision and all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in your lap, then opens his eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lift the eyelid with your hand, then grasp the nail with small, double-pronged forceps, and extend it upwards;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put on it a horsehair, or a cow's hair, or an ox hair, and a strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the nail, and pierce it completely with the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and extend it upwards, and scrape away with the hair the side of the nail which follows the pupil and the silk with the hair to the head, then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct with a fine spatula and small forceps, and leave the natural flesh at the tear duct, so that the body of the tears does not come out through the incision habitually;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the nail is extended only with the hook and the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then scrape it with a smooth spatula of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And take care that the spatula does not touch and break the fleshy membrane, and that the pupil is not pierced;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, pour into the eye a little crushed salt, and of the collyrium made from litharge, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not sinewy, and you cannot insert the needle, and the hooks cannot enter, many times this type of nail is cured with medicines;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you wish to cut it, open the patient's eye, and take the spatula, slightly sharp, according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And scrape the nail thinly, and if you see that it diminishes somewhat and the erosion is pressing there, then distil from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made from litharge and the red collyrium and crushed salt, and plug the eye until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then recommence the other work according to this same method, until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then recommence the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh of the tear duct harms the eye by great irritation, then suspend it with an oncin, and cut a part of it and not all of it, so that the tear duct is not affected;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	then instill into the eye a red collyrium which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In the eyes of some men, sometimes red flesh grows, and covers the pupil and encroaches on the eyelids and turns them inside out, and resembles a pomegranate rose;
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the procedure is that the patient puts his head in your lap, then opens his eyes, and you pull all that flesh with hooks suitable for this, and support it firmly;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first flesh, and keep cutting with a razor to the end, and be careful that you do not injure the eye during the procedure;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision be with the spatula that we have mentioned in the incision of the nail and with small forceps with which one removes the felon, as the figure after this chapter demonstrates;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, apply crushed  oil of celandine or you may distill red copperas and similar corrosive medicines there, and apply a cotton pad over the eye with egg white, so that it is secure from a hot abscess;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if anything remains, and the hot blood overwhelms you, and you fear a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with things that soothe hot abscesses;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do when flesh is added to the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But however, it is necessary that you ease the treatment of each weak eye by the natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and by the accidental way, in the work of iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand to any of these works until you see that the limb is able to endure that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Sebel are red veins that are covered over the eye, and they hinder the sight in its work and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is necessary then first that you look if the eye, in which the sebel is, is strong, and there is no other illness except the sebel;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then treat the eye in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then you suspend those veins with the unguent according to your wisdom, and let the unguent be finely divided according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two unguents by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then one treats forcefully those veins subtly, and wipes away the blood one time after another, until you see those veins removed from the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and take care that you do not injure the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at midday before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you cut only those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, then instill into the eye green and red gall to corrupt that which remains of the pus.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you are not able to remove all of it at that time, then apply a plaster to the eye of things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for a few days until the pain is eased and the abscess is assured to be warm, then begin again in this manner which is before until it is healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the method of treatment:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The Arabs call a fistula "arissati":
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you treat it with cautery and with burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then it is necessary that you lance the abscess where it should mature, and draw out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then scrape it all with the instrument of which this is the form;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "rough head," and it should be made of hard iron with a round head, and it should be pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that this corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the place is healed, and flesh grows there, and the body of the bone is healed, and remains so for forty days, and it does not renew itself and is not abscessed, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	if not, there is no other device than to return the fistula to the opening of the nose according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take a drill according to this form, and let the head of iron have three angles, and let the shaft be tapered to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand a little away from the eye, then turn the drill completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because the wind comes out if he holds his hand over his nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the place hardens, the matter goes to the nose;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	this is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the discharge from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are completely open, and there is no obstruction or diminution in the nose, you must bind the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then cleanse it, then apply cupping glasses or scarification without wounding to draw out the humor, then apply to the eye a liniment made of acacia, and aloe, and incense, and sarcocolla, and then bandage the eye, and apply a plaster of bandages and cloths;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the cloths is that you take sufficiently soft cloths, and double each one fourfold, and then place one upon another according to the quantity that the eye requires;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then bind it over with a strong bandage, and repeat the cupping to draw out the humor without wounding;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye bandaged day and night, and if the liniment softens, you must bandage it tightly;
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the liniment after a day and a night, and if you see the eye repairing, it is good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then repeat the plaster and cloths and the liniment and the cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the rupture of a webbed membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When a rupture occurs in the webbed membrane, then it opens, and there comes forth matter like grains of resin, and it is frightful to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see it opened, the procedure is such that you insert a needle into the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the part of the tear;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and pierce it there, and leave the first needle in place;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the double thread and tie a part of the membrane around it, and pull it well, then remove the needle and apply to the eye wool soaked in egg white;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the thread falls away with the membrane, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and sometimes the wound is restrained by the membrane on all sides by a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye protrudes greatly, pierce it with a fine spatula that reaches deep into the eye, and correct the whitish moisture and the eye descends, and it enters immediately;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the arch of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a swelling that is gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, and it is not water;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of the procedure is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands on two sides, and move it until you see the swelling come above your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then let it be pierced, and let the light not descend and be obstructed, and let the patient see things as he was used to;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the swelling is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	then make the patient sit between your hands, then take a thin spatula and make an incision on the cornea a little bit along the conjunctiva with the cornea and the iris, until the swelling comes out;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is out, then instill warm water mixed with honey into the eye, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and honey, then let it be treated with other treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have just now the similarities of the waters in the division, and what is necessary for piercing;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	then work according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and bind the healthy eye and bind it very tightly;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	then place the point of the instrument next to the cornea by the thickness of a ray in that whiteness of the eye at the part of the lesser tear, then push the instrument which is called "almagda" skillfully, and turn your hand until it pierces the whiteness of the eye, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty thing;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda's path be at the depth of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and that is the cornea of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	then you will see the bone in that membrane because of the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then place the instrument to the place where the water is, then press it from below one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the water descends immediately, the patient sees in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	Afterwards, rest a little, and if the water rises the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is inserted and it does not rise, then extract the almagda lightly by turning your hand little by little;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put back in water a little rock salt, and lift with this the eye inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put on top of the eye tampons or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white, and bind with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on top crushed cumin with egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which here is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And pierce then only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle place, then put in the almagda, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a suitable sleeping-place, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and let him be free from all movement, and take light foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let him be bound according to his condition until the third day;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then unbind him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not necessary that you do this at the time of the treatment or immediately after the incision, but it is necessary that you delay this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	if a warm abscess comes, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and treat it with that which soothes the abscess;
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is calmed, then unbind the sight and put on his face a small pillow to cover for a few days, and let him always be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then let him go out of the house little by little, and return to his usual activities;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from Iraq, who told us that in his country they made almond-flavored something, to which one added water, but still I never saw any in our land, nor did I ever read of it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almonds, so that those who do not know them may see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and let them be properly of bronze:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of them be of this same thinness, and the last in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes there grow on the nose added various fleshy growths, of which some resemble scorpions with many feet;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and there are some where there is cancerous flesh of a livid color, and there is soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that then of these fleshes which is soft, and not cancerous, it is necessary that you cause the patient to sit between your hands against the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open his nostrils, and cast the onion on those fleshes, and pull them out;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then cut what you can hold with a thin, sharp spatula on one side, until you know that that flesh is all removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains that cannot be cut, open it completely with the finest instruments lightly, so that nothing remains;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if blood overflows, or an abscess forms, treat it as is necessary;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is a malignant abscess, hurry and cauterize it until the blood is stopped and all the flesh is removed, then pour in vinegar and water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the nose works, and moisture comes down to the palate, know that it is healed;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not flow as it should, know that there is new flesh on the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach to cut:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then you must insert a rather thick linen thread, knotted at both ends, with a finger-width or less space between each knot;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and let the patient put the end of the thread in his nose as far as possible, and pull gently until it comes through the nose into the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for one who wishes to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the end that comes through the nose in one hand, and the other end that comes through the mouth in the other hand, and pull each alternately, sawing at the knots which are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you see that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and reinsert it into the nose as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then place in the nose a lead tube for a few days until it is healed, and if there is need of drying medicines, then use them;
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, with which one instills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And let it be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the conduit likewise;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full to purge the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have a handle at the top for holding it when one heats the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh above the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease arises at the head of the nose which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large constantly, until it is a dreadful thing to behold;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and therefore it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and remove it entirely, then apply to the place the cautery or burning medicine;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if one delays cutting it until it is large, then take care if it is hard, of livid color, insensitive:
