car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it re-enters the flesh, and causes an abscess and putrefaction in the place, and a bad illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for which reason it is necessary that it be treated little by little to the end, and that nothing remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and sometimes this vein, when it is treated, is five palms long, or ten, and a man once came to me, from whom it emerged ten palms long, and when you cut it, put a probe in the opening, and pierce it to the bottom, so that everything comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and let the matter that is inside be emptied, and administer to the place medicines preventing putrefaction for some days, then cure it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein has many roots, and especially when it appears in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and there are many openings, from which pus flows;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	cure it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of the worms which are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This illness is called in our land "ox disease," because it often happens to oxen, and is a small worm which is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body rising and falling, and one feels it well going from limb to limb, until it breaks the skin where it goes, and pus flows;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is engendered by the corruption of certain humors, just as worms and serpents and lumbríci and ascárides are in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance it enters, and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it to cure and pull, then one can only pull it out when it moves:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong ligature tightly, then cut it above and pull it out, and if the worm is deep in the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does, is that it runs to the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming to the head near the eye, then press down firmly on the eyebrow below it, then cut above, and pull it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to treat the patient with bodily cleansing with purgative medicines for the bad putrid humors, and to abstain from foods causing putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and a little later, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departed from that place, and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then a little later ran throughout the body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it constantly turned around her body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I greatly marveled how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had seen many who had felt pain move from place to place, but I had not seen it as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and the veins uncovered, and because of this, that constrained windiness appeared;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear for this reason in those who are plump, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you wish to cure this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears as we have said, then bind it above and below quickly, and then cut above until that constrained windiness escapes from the place;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure it with that which expels windiness, such as fetid pills, and pills of serapinum, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their diversity is that there are some which have large points, and small ones, and barbed ones, and smooth ones;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some that have two angles, and some that have barbs, and some which are broken;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which falls in a limb falls in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it then falls in any of these members, and the signs of death, which I shall tell you hereafter, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must avoid extracting this arrow, for death follows in many ways;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these bad signs do not appear, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then I draw it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the signs of injury to the brain when the arrow falls there and pierces the bone, and the dura mater which is over the brain is injured, are when there is scotoma and thirst and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps blood flows from the nostrils, or from the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps he loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound comes a white moisture resembling pus, and also something like shreds of flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear, abstain from treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs that the arrow has struck the heart are that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it were fixed in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow moves like pus, and dark blood flows, and there is coldness and cold sweat, and syncope;
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	know then without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs that the arrow has injured the lung are that frothy spittle comes from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs deeply and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow strikes the covering of the breast, it is near the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and he breathes heavily and feels great pain and sighs;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the muscles of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, perhaps something of the undigested food comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly, and some dung comes out through the ruptured intestine, there is no hope of cure, nor of extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow strikes the bladder, and urine comes out and flows, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the arm and the spine of the back and the breastbone and the thigh and the legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I shall tell you happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the tear duct at the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it, and drew it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I drew out at one time an arrow that struck him in the fatty tissue of the eye under the eyelid; and the arrow was embedded, and I could reach only the point towards the shaft, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, with a light iron head without barbs;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	the man was healed, and no ill effects came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with barbs:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I sawed the barbs, and worked so delicately that I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I drew an arrow from a man, which had fallen into his belly, and I thought that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then when thirty days had passed, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the arrow, and grasped it, and drew it forth, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw a man from whom an arrow fell into his back, and the wound was closed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and he did not change his natural disposition, nor did he find harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, into whose face an arrow fell, and the wound was closed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and it remained so without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And I extracted an arrow from a man of the king's princes, which had fallen into his nose, and was slightly leaning towards the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat it after it had fallen in three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched it with a very fine probe, and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a prick and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought that it was from the point of the arrow. I applied an attractive and digestive plaster to the place, so that the place would not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the place of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the plaster there for many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained thus for a long time, until one day he felt the arrow within his nose;
et il le me dist.	and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied a sharp corrosive medicine to the wound for many days, until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which was sticking in the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I added to the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared to me visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and a period of about four months passed, and then I widened the wound so that I inserted the forceps, and moved it from one side to the other, but it could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I did not cease to refine and devise means of instruments, until I took it one day with well-made forceps, according to what its form will be at the end of this chapter, until I extracted it, and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the surgeons judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you apply your care to what I do not say, for a book cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise master learns from very little, and from what is present and lacking to him, finds new work, and a new instrument, for the treatment of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out of the limbs where they are fixed except according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either by the place where they entered, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which leaps out by the place where it entered, that is an arrow entering fleshy places, and sometimes leaping out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not leap out immediately, leave it until the flesh around it is rotten, and the exit is made easier;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot come out, leave it thus for some days, and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will leap out, and if it does not leap out, pierce all around with a thin drill, until the place around is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear in the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not pull it out, but leave it until it is loose after some days, for if the arrow reaches the dura mater, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is fixed only in the bone, and does not reach the dura mater, and the patient remains some days without bad symptoms, devise a way to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply fixed thus and cannot come out easily, apply terebration around it, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the body such that one cannot see it, search for it with a tent.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, pull it out with a suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, enlarge the wound;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has barbs by which it holds, remove the flesh that is pierced on both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrow, until you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow, as you would then remove it with greater difficulty.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, leave it until the surrounding area is rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood hinders you, use what we have said in its chapter concerning treatment;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting the nerve and the vein, and devise a way how you can remove the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and position the patient as he was when the arrow entered, for that is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then position him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, where something of it is visible, or the skin is swollen where it is clearly seen or felt:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut above it, until the forceps can grasp it, and then extract it:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it leaps out immediately.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, rotate your hand round and round until it enters the bone and widens it, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for a while, and then resume extraction until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is there, remove it with the whole shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft breaks, and you wish to administer extraction, use a hollow instrument so that the point of the arrow enters the hollow of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then pull it out, and if the arrow is broken, use a pointed instrument going in, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow breaks in the foot or in the belly or in the bladder or in the side, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut to it, cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut a vein or a nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one extracts arrows resembles a bird's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many kinds:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pushing head is like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrow, as here is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the forceps for pushing and for pulling is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins from which one is bled, of which there are 16 in the head, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two temples which are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are apparent in the two temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins which are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the upper lip of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and the lay people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the lay people call it "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side, and the lay people call it "vein of the belly", and it is on the forearm, and it is the one from which one bleeds, which clearly appears on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the salvatiella is the vein which is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and in the foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the bend of the wrist on the left side, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein which is called "nase", which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	Bleeding from the veins that are behind the ears helps with old cataracts and with migraine;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the bleeding, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then the patient constricts his neck with a bandage, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places hanging from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then seek them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, bleed from there;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and put it under the vein down to the bone, then raise your hand with the entire vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein well two fingers across, and let out blood as much as you wish;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then constrain and bind it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already discussed incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	Bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for chronic migraine, and toothache, and habitual ophthalmia, and for a flow of hot tears from the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the bloodletting is as I said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient should constrict his neck, until the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse under your finger, and then bleed from there;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the skin above the vein up to your index finger, and put the lancet underneath, and lift the vein up, and cup it, as you have done in the two other veins, and let blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then unbind the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	Bleeding from the frontal vein is as effective as bleeding from the cephalic vein for old facial ailments, and for migraine, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called a "lancet," of which here is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you wish;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then untie the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed, and sometimes the work is done with a broad blade.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it is not necessary that the blade be too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and cut across, for the bone is near, and perhaps the blade will break when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bloodletting of the two veins that are in the two temples helps with them, and with ringworm, and with redness, and with hordeolum in the eye, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bloodletting is that the patient constricts his neck by twisting with some linen, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then bleed him, and let the bloodletting be across, a little of the length of the blade a little wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the blade is thin, perhaps it will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then let the blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind on cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	Bleeding from the vein of the nose is good for fever, and for raging thirst, and for facial illnesses, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is chronic;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the manner of bleeding is that the patient grasps his neck, then you hold his nose with your left hand, and take a long, thin blade, and insert it between the lips in the space that is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not appear well there, and the blood will immediately begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it overnight, for it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the blade:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	Bleeding from the two temples helps with shortness of breath, and the beginning of leprosy, and many illnesses, and impetigo, and toothache, and herpes, and fistulas;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the manner of bleeding is that the patient grasps his neck under one side and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the master stand over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then open the vein lengthwise a little broadly, then draw blood moderately, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then do likewise in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and bind both veins moderately, so that the patient does not choke;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until morning, that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the bleeding of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bleeding from the veins of the upper lip helps with a boil in the mouth, and with corruption of the gums, and fissures of the lips, and of the nose and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is to make the patient sit before you, and bind his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, of which one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known because they are black, and because around them are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	cut then one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then cut the largest on each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Bleeding from the veins that are under the tongue helps after bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and lifts his tongue, and looks underneath on each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	bleed then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck from which one commonly bleeds are bled according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by piercing with a completely flat, wide blade, or an olive-shaped, thin one like a cutting lancet, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flat blade is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening the full neck veins of thick, apparent blood, and which contain thick and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive-shaped blade:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the thin veins, where there is thin, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	Bleeding from the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the bleeder that he bleeds wisely, and that he guards against the artery which is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the lancet should not be pointed, but cutting like a chisel.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica vein does not appear clearly, then it is necessary that you search for it, and choose another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you seek a branch of it, or you bleed in its place the vein in the middle of the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it appears clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut with a chisel-shaped lancet, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place of the bleeding, it is necessary that you extend the arm, that you touch the place until you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with ink, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the chisel-shaped lancet;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and beware that you do not strike the artery when you see the place swollen, for that is the artery:
eschui la donques.	wipe it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it spurt upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hasten yourself then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, which often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	if it is the arm, bind it, and leave it thus, and let the patient not move it;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be without fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood is not stanched, and it overcomes you, and medicine is not at hand, then cut the artery if it is visible, for the head of it retracts;
et estainche li sans.	and stanch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of bark from a fig tree, and split it, and take one of the halves and bind it on well until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the blood stanches, it is well;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then treat it, as we have said, with powders that stanch blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stanching is not difficult in many cases because of the small size of the wound, and the power of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The bloodletting of the vein in the middle helps because it draws blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the phlebotomist to be careful of the nerve which is below, and if he goes too deep, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the bleeding is difficult, and perhaps cannot be healed;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men because of its subtlety, then you must bleed it with a lancet;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid the nerve to your ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	Bleeding from the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed by puncturing the olivary vein or the myrtle vein, for this is the safest of all veins, because beneath it there is neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, one must seek the lightest place, and it matters not if one fails the first time, and one begins again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and perhaps the place swells in some men, when one fails the first time, but it matters not.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that bloodletting is administered only to preserve health, and to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins that are in the neck:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, median, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed at the beginning of spring fasting, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first day or the third, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bloodletting which is administered for illnesses has no determined hour, but when need is, by day or by night, at all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not fitting to bleed children until fourteen years, nor a woman carrying a child except from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should the elderly who have passed sixty years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that he cleanse the intestines with a light clyster, if he has much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the putrid superfluities harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should one bleed him who is too full of food, nor who is drunk, until he is sober, nor those with dropsy;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and one should beware of bleeding after a colic attack, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and frequent intercourse with a woman, and toil, wakefulness and fasting, and anything that weakens, whether by something of the mind or of the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then thin the humors, if the blood is thick, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood, and bleed him from the vein of the arm around the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep him that day from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be cheerful and happy, and let the bleeder be higher than the one being bled, and let him rub the arm two or three times, then tie the ligature moderately above, for when it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the place with the hands, until the veins swell, and one feels them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then the bleeder moistens the lancet with a little old oil, then puts his finger of his left hand on that vein below the place a little where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not slip and escape when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee like strings when being bled, and there are some that are full of wind, so that when one puts on the lancet, it withdraws from the lancet, and cannot open the vein, and so it is with those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the bleeder must be skilled in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then begin again a little below that place or above quickly, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is swollen, and the patient is frightened, leave it a day or two, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	by chance, an abscess will form there;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	and do not enter the bath, then resume bleeding if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that enough blood will come out as you wish, then thrust into that same opening with the whole blade straight;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work somewhat quickly, before the place becomes swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not resume bleeding, and put on a little of lye of oil, for it lightens the body of the blood, and lye is milder in this place than oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the lye of oil in each bleeding that you bleed the veins, to staunch the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same thing does theriac and ox-gall, when one puts it on the place;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so it thins the blood and it separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if a large abscess forms there, which happens many times, especially when it is not bled except at that time when the opening of the vein is small, hurry, and put on the place a sponge soaked in water and a little warm vinegar, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if there remains at the place after some days some blackness or greenness, it does not harm;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you wish, put on something of aloes or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, mint, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times an abscess and appearance occur at the bleeding of the basilica vein:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Then put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the compression of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Avoid then that you put on nothing of that which we have said, for perhaps it cuts off the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but make a dry plaster for it to harden the place, then cure it with another cure, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each one blood according to the quantity of his strength, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let out so much until it is red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it out until it is thinned;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, that a larger wound be made for him, and the lancet be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him little and often, and one should bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of bleeding is safe from the flow of blood and the cutting of nerves, and is better than bleeding lengthwise or across.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to one whose body fails during bleeding, it is necessary to give bread soaked in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if he is heated, draw blood three or four times. And if he is of cold complexion, let him eat before bleeding bread soaked in quince syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during bleeding, after the loss of much blood, it is necessary that he drink broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the opening of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm, and bleed another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to bleed from another place, should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	therefore it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and widen the opening until it flows in a stream;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then, when you observe all the conditions of bleeding, and place your hand on his pulse while he bleeds, that death may not come instead of a stream, and this happens many times, when the bleeder is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary, when you wish to untie the arm, and cause blood to flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is curved, that he extend the arm hastily, for that would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him be until he bleeds a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you prick it with the point of a flame, until the blood which is congealed at the opening of the vein flows out freely, and put on it a little salt dissolved in water, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not bind it, until the abscess is subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is need to draw blood a second time, bleed him in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled in place of the vein in the head because it is composed [in a similar way].
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in warm water until the vein is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it is bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then bleed it immediately across, not across the width or length;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and bleed very near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, put the hand back in warm water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for one puts it in more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	Bleeding from the salvatory vein of the right hand is good for all liver diseases, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	constrict the hand, and put it in warm water until the vein is swollen, so that one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it bleeds across, and if you cut it completely through, it does no harm;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too deep, for the nerves are underneath, completely bare of flesh, and then put the hand back in warm water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is needed, put oil and salt on the vein to quickly cauterize, and do so for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Bleeding from the left hand is good for the disease of the head, and do just as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Bleeding from the saphena vein is good for all the illnesses that are in the lower body, such as diseases of the womb, and the retention of menses, and disease of the kidneys, and of the thighs and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of this bleeding is that the patient puts his foot in warm water, and rubs the vein until it swells, and binds above the joint of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot many branches go;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	bleed then from the largest branch, or at the ankle, which is most effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you bleed it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and bleed across as if cutting;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the blade be sharp.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot flow out, put the foot in water, and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the bleeding fails the first time, start again a little higher up, for the place is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do the same for the saphenous vein of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle, and bleeding it is good for hip pain, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of its bleeding is such that the patient enters the bath, and presses above the ankle with four fingers twisting, because otherwise the vein does not appear;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it appears, bleed it in every way that you can, and across;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, because the location is safe, and it is very abundant in many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, bleed any vein that appears on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make as much blood flow as you wish, and then untie the ligature, and apply cotton and bind it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of the bleedings of cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cups are made of horn, or of brass, or of glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and venesection is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this venesection which is without cutting is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is with fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and venesection which is done by cutting and by the extraction of blood is done in fourteen places of the body, of which one is at the very top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is in the middle of the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others on the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping below the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cupping on the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping above the buttocks;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cuppings between the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cuppings on the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cuppings on the two ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and cupping does not draw blood except from the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken one, as bleeding from a vein does;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be administered, either with fire or without fire, in any illness that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to cup, or for custom, then we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle, and at every time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see at night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is mid-month, we order cupping after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bloodletting of the temple helps the headache... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this cupping is in place of bloodletting from the cephalic vein, and it is not necessary that one who is of cold complexion use it, or who has a catarrh, for it does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not necessary that the elderly use it, nor those who have cold diseases in the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who is often bled in this way becomes forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping a little lower because of the danger of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Cupping in the neck is in place of bloodletting from the head and the basilic vein, and therefore it is good for the constriction of the chest, and for a fissure in the windpipe, and for cough, and for repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be applied lightly, for if it holds too firmly, it causes forgetfulness or harm to the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Cupping at the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, and ophthalmia and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in place of bloodletting from the basilic vein;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you must instruct the bleeder to extend the arm when applying the cups, so that he does not cut the artery and cause a great flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	Cupping under the chin is good for mouth diseases, and for corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is in place of bloodletting from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping of the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	Cupping of the elbows is as good as three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from those large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the physician not to go too deep, for the place is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass that is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the rectum, and for diseases below, and the cupping glass must be large, and of brass, that it may draw well;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and perchance, if it were thin, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The cupping glasses of the legs are manifestly healing, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the loins, and of the womb, and of the bladder, and they restore the menses;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are placed on the two shinbones, and the two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting in many constitutions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of applying the cupping glass is that you first place it empty, and suck moderately, and place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing this, until you see the place red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then heat, and reapply the cupping glasses, and take heed of the constitution of the bodies, for there are some who have tender flesh, and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deep;
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to refine the passage of thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw blood little by little, one time is sufficient.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, we begin again often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the limit is that the heart be pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cupping glasses with aperitive and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, with cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
