Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take wormwood oil, or balm oil, or dill oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one whom one heals has tender flesh and large pores, then it is not necessary to put any oil there, but it should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or nightshade water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And the one who has much moisture, should be washed with vinegar, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick excesses should be washed with old wine, or beet juice, or a decoction of dill or chamomile, or others similar;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and one should not use cupping before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath, one or two hours;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he be careful, when he is to be cupped and when he is cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the one who is being treated is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	then he should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with vinegar, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat chicken, and mutton, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, should take honey syrup, and moderately fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat chicken and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day that he is cupped, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men sometimes theriac or nutmeg before or after cupping, to strengthen the principal members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and the blood should be thinned, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cupping glasses which are applied without cutting are those which are applied to the liver, and to the spleen, and gout, and to the belly and the breast and the kidneys and the hip, for these members do not tolerate being cut, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, just as we apply them to the breasts when the milk flows;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity which is in the member, just as we apply cupping glasses to the belly and to the breast to soften the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and removes the pain, when there is obstruction or stone, it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and so it does when it is applied to the liver and to the spleen when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are applied empty to suck only;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are applied with fire, and sometimes full of warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass applied with fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let it be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and let it have on the side around the middle a small hole, as for inserting a needle, and let it be of bronze, smooth in front so that it does not wound the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let it have in the middle a crossbar of bronze or iron, to put a burning candle in, and let there be large and small ones according to the illnesses and the age of those who receive them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of old people, and of thin people from those of fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus place this cupping glass on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the candle of wax or a liniment, and put it into the cupping glass across the bar which is in the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and your fingers should be on the hole that we have mentioned, so that when one wants, the vapor goes out, and one removes the cupping glass;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and one takes the liniment as before, and repeats it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass then, which is administered in the illness of pleurisy, with hot water, there is no bar or hole, and it is not administered except when it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb only;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leech application is only administered to limbs where cupping glasses cannot be applied due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in places devoid of flesh, such as fingers or nose, and others similar;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the leech is that when you find leeches that are in clean fresh water without putrefaction, you should take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them for a night in fresh water, until they are hungry and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then having bled the vein and cupped, then rub the limb until it is red, and apply the leeches;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where one can apply a cupping glass, apply it, for this is very beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the place with vinegar, and then with water, very well, and then sprinkle it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place bleeds too much after the leeches fall off, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and apply it, until the bleeding is stopped;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the bleeding is profuse, apply crushed vitriol, or galls, and similar things, until it is stopped;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you may place on the area halves of peeled beans, and leave them until they dry on the area; this will stop the bleeding immediately;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, apply more leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the leeches will not attach, rub the area with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until blood flows, and then apply them; as soon as they sense the blood, they will attach;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they fall off, sprinkle a little aloe and salt, crushed, or ashes, on them; they will fall off immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the foolish scoff at this chapter, for they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor read any letter of them;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is diminished in our land, for I never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except through the science of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have drawn the science from them, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter that which is contained, and I have shortened it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary, then, that we say in the prologue of this book the sum of the words and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or contusion comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to bleed the patient on one side and the other, if nothing prevents you, such as weakness of body, or an infant, or an old man;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the time is not very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold foods, that is to say cold pottage, and the flesh of birds and of kids, and let him not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and let him not fill himself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no fear of a hot abscess, or of the spread of matter to the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	then let the patient return to his former regimen that he had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with foods that produce great nourishment, or that have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and tripe of a cow, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the flesh grows again and the fracture heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of old and decrepit people cannot be well mended or healed according to their nature because of the dryness of their limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is a cure, reset the broken bone with thick bandages that support and join the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not cease from this work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish him with strong foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the breast, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes across, and another lengthwise, like the shaft of a writing pen.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with only a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type has its own device and proper instrument in its restoration, according to what the memory brings to its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and a fracture of the bone is known because the place is twisted, and it appears clearly by swelling, and sounds when pressed by the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or sound on touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but there may well be a twisting, or fissure, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Then you must not move it by hand, but apply the medicines that follow, and then hold it firmly and subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that for a fracture that goes spirally, and the two parts are disjointed, you must immediately set them evenly, so that abscesses do not form there;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot abscesses form there, leave it for a few days, until the abscesses are subsided;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it evenly so that you can gently and wisely move it, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restoration of one where there are pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold it, as is necessary later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces, extend it from two sides, if it is the hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural form, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you bring back by all means the additions to their places as best you can, and ensure that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	then straighten it nicely, and do not bind it too tightly, nor press it as those do who cause by their work a hot abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, instruct the patient well not to move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor by turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels any pain, it is not in place, and it must be put in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is put straight, so that no crookedness comes when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in size and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	then it is necessary to wrap it with soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	then it is necessary to wrap it with a wide and strong linen, for the wide linen embraces the whole large limb, and constricts it equally on all sides, so that there is no slack;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then bind around light tow, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little on the whole linen, then go above the fracture and tighten less, so that the fracture may then remove the fracture a little;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the linen little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy area, then take another linen, and turn it around again over the broken area;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the fracture, and bind moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the linen bandages tow or cloths, until it is all even, then bind all over with a bandage, and then apply your well-made splints, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then apply something that soothes a hot abscess, and which removes the swelling, and leave it thus for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then bind on your splints, and let them be half of a wisely sawn broad cane, or of wood from which cleavers are made, or of palm branches, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint that one places on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let it also be as long as is necessary for the limb, small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind on the splints as you did in the first binding, then bind over it a suitable thread, as in the first binding over the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	tighter above, always less so;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their bandages of twisted linen cords, and this is a great error, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too thin, and it is not necessary that there be less than the width of a finger between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the ends of the splints after the tightening in healthy places, then put under them linen or carded wool padding, so that he is not injured.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind all broken limbs with splints on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to apply splints except after five days or seven, or more depending on your certainty of a hot abscess developing;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And here is the manner of the ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take the flour that adheres to the walls of the mill, and cook it with plenty of egg, and apply this confection, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture in many conditions, and especially for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take 3 parts of barley and ladanum and enula and asafoetida and gum arabic and mugwort, of each 10 parts;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloes, of each 5 parts;
alechil VIIII З.;	comfrey 9 parts;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make them into a powder, and mix them with egg white;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the man's complexion is warm, he should use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is of use to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another kind of plaster that is good for a sprain:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mugwort and mallow, each 10 parts;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloes, each 9 parts;
acaice VI З.;	acacia 6 parts;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Armenian bole 10 parts, and grind well, and mix with water or egg white, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another type of plaster for joints and bones dislocated from their place, and soothes the resulting pain, and the splintering and breakage of the bone:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new wool, and moisten it in vinegar and boiled oil, and apply it to the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly removes the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another type of plaster which restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and leaves of ground poppy, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another type of plaster for the restoration of a bone fracture and to diminish the remainder of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take mallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, bean flour, one part of each;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is inflamed, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another type of plaster stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take mallow roots, and flaxseed, balausta, melilot, and comfrey, and violet and chamomile flowers, of all these one part each;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb for restoration except a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to think that one should put on a broken limb, for restoration, slightly warm dry things, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another kind of plaster which is good for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and cut human hair, or bird feathers, and mallow, and mix them equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and bind it on.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then unbind it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, and that the bone has not moved from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if not, unbind it in several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain or itching comes to the place, or restlessness or swelling, hasten, and unbind it, and remove the plaster immediately;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a wet sea sponge, and dip it in water, and bathe the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it on a nut, until you are sure of a warm abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and the inflammation of the limb will subside, and the pain will be removed, then recommence the subtle binding, and a little of the plaster, and do not bind it so tightly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and continue until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess and redness and pain and swelling are completely gone, and you need plaster and binding, then recommence it, as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, then do not unbind it before III or IIII or V or VII days;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture mends, and the joining of the flesh approaches;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then bind it more tightly than before, and it thickens its flesh, as I said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the place drying more than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot come to it;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then moisten it with lukewarm water, every time you unbind it, and that should be every third day, and loosen the binding a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this work then nourishment flows to the limb, and quickly mends what the foolish healers do, who bind the limb too tightly:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	that is bad, and it is a dangerous practice, and I see nothing else but leaving it alone and working correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the diverse manners of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures there are, and diverse forms, and the causes are different;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures that are made by the blow of a sword, and the neck breaks the whole bone down to the spongy bone which is beneath the bone, as does a hatchet or club;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason this manner of fracture is called "hatchet-fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blunt impact, or a fissure, or a neck-fracture from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or from similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which reaches down to the membrane which is under the bone, or which is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound which is located in the bone as fine as a hair, and the fissure is small, and therefore this fracture is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound which is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and causes a piece of the bone to enter, and the place is swollen as the cauldrons do when they are struck.
si entre li piere dedens.	If the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in the head, such as the heads of children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these types of fractures that small pieces are separated like stars;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by the pulling on them, and the probing with probes, and by the corrupted flesh which is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like resemblance is known by this, that when the bone has been uncovered, and one rubs against it, the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, pay attention to the accidents of the patient, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of consciousness, and extension, and faintness, and acute fever, and the eyes protruding and reddening, and other similar things in many conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no frightening accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, and it is in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day, if you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the flesh under the bone is corrupted, and the accidents that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the fractured part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover the bone in every way that you can, and the area of the wound as gently as possible, and if bleeding occurs upon uncovering the bone, or a hot abscess, help him with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the area with cloths moistened in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed, and you are assured of the cessation of bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of working:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one method is that you cut with a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you make a number of different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and should be of tempered iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly, so that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is strong and hard, then you must pierce it around, before you make incisions with a trephine, not so deeply that it pierces through the skull bone, and it should have above the point a margin or a circle, which prevents the point from passing beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have several, so that each comes in its place on the thickness of the bone, so that you have trephines for the whole head;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three types of trephines:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The method for piercing around the fractured bone is that you place a trephine on the bone, and turn it with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put the trephine elsewhere a little afterwards, and so do all around, then cut with the incisors the thickness of the bone which is between the holes, and do this as subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you remove the bone with your hand, or with some of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and take care that you do not touch the brain or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and removed the bone, it is necessary that you smooth the remaining portion of bone with another instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other incisors;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if any small bones or splinters remain, remove them lightly with one of the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of operation is that which Galen described, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he praised it greatly, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must uncover a part of the bone where the broken place appears, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under the head of this lenticular incisor, of which this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut on one side, and the part is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small mallet above, so that you cut the bone lightly all around, and take good care of the membrane that is below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is attached to the bone, remove it gently, for it is removed well without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then you must smooth that roughness, and remove the splinters with a fine rasp of which you should have various sizes, to apply in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	First use large rasps, and then finer ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hairline fractures and subtle breaks, you must apply treatment according to its condition;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is not readily known to one who has not applied himself to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the synovial membrane is exposed, then you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled over two or three times, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as gently as you can, so that you do not injure the synovial membrane, then apply another bandage over it, and do not bind it tightly except so that it holds the wound only;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it thus for one or two days, until the swelling of the abscess is subsided, then unbind it, and apply medicines such as lily roots, and bean flour, and incense powder, and birthwort, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and apply frequently cleansing medicines without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and guard that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave ointment there, nor let pus gather there, for when pus gathers on the brain’s membrane, it corrupts and rots it, and great harm comes to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one puts something biting on the synovial membrane, it becomes necrotic on top.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness comes there only because of the medicine that has been put on, which has such a property, then you must take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and glue one cloth, and put it on the synovial membrane;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with the appropriate treatments, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose are broken above, or one by itself, for these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, except by bending or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must put your little finger in the nostril, and set the broken part against your index finger, and the little finger on the outside, until the nose returns to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the place, then you must set it with the end of a somewhat thick stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, do likewise, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling of the abscess has subsided, then put into the nostrils tents of linen cloths, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you place one on the other side, if the fracture is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the tents be so large that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one should moisten the tents in butter, and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but they must be moistened in a mixture of egg white and mill dust;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the tent until the bone is strong and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes one puts goose feathers in the nose instead of tents, and a soft cloth is wrapped around it, and the fracture is held, and the patient blows through it;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do whatever you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come to the nose while you are working there, put cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil, or a little diachylon there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if hot abscesses do not come there, apply a plaster externally, of chickpea flour and incense powder, cooked with egg white, then put light lint on top, and do not bind the nose;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with instruments suitable for this, then sew the fissure, and treat it with things that generate flesh and that solder, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents, and put lead canulae in it, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken underneath, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only external and is not broken in two, except perhaps inwardly, it is easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left jaw, put your index finger of the right hand, and gently put the fracture back in place, and adjust it with the other hand from the outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension from two sides, until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or breakage, bind them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then apply cerate to the broken jaw, and apply a double cloth;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and put on the cloth a well-made large star, or a piece of leather even, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape changes, unbind it on the third day, and then readjust what has changed;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a plaster, of mill powder with egg white or bean flour, after you have removed the cerate;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put light wool on the plaster, and if the plaster dries, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	often it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses occur, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, observe if any piece of the bone is removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	then carefully remove it with the instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with a blade according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, sew up the wound, if it is wide, and apply suitable plasters to it, to generate flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the fracture
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fracture often breaks in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and separated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the procedure is, when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the broken fracture;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then set the fracture with your fingers, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, then place under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth, or of wool, and let it be large according to your need;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and lift the collarbone, and pull the sphere with your hand, so that you set the fracture, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the collarbone outwards, because it goes in deeply, then the patient must lie often on his back, and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and the attendant pushes the shoulder down, until the bone of the collarbone is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then set the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it broken, then you must cut it open;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and draw out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join because of some obstacle, then cut it with one of the scalpels that you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you place this instrument under the collarbone, to protect the viscera:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not sharp, and should be as wide as is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the operation;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two ends, as you see, and one is wide, and the other narrow, as is the opening of the wound that you have made when you have drawn out the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the opening is small, or you suspect a hot abscess, then fill the wound with lint and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses appear, moisten a piece of lint in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you apply to the bone a plaster of ground powder and egg white, and place light tampons on top, and place a splint under the armpit, if you need it;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very wide bandage, a handspan wide, then place a double layer of cloth over the tampons and the plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a thin strip three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the end of the bandage is hanging;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the strip on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the affected armpit;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and tighten it on each side, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the strip does not move on the broken bone, then check it each day, and when the bandage loosens, then tighten it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the armpit when he sleeps, to raise the shoulder;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	this will lighten the fracture of the collarbone by the elevation of the shoulder, or you bind his arm to his neck, and do not unbind it unless a bad accident occurs, up to twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then renew the plaster, if you see that it is necessary, and tighten it and leave it so, until he is healed;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is healed at most in twenty-eight days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It happens that the shoulder breaks either at the large part or in the middle, and one knows it only by the touch;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	then set it according to the form of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the place powdered millstone with abundant egg white, and light tampons, and put on top a double cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place on top a broad and thin splint, a little larger than the shoulder, and if underneath the splint the hair is tangled in any part of the shoulder, then fill that hair with linen tampons, so that the splint sits evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it all with a strong bandage firmly, so that the splint does not move from its place, and examine the binding each day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time that it loosens, then bind it, and set the splint evenly if it is out of place, and let the patient lie on his side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in twenty or twenty-five days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number of days is complete, then unbind it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that easily dislocates.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward, and points below the heart, then incise and remove it, and do what we have said in the fracture of the clavicle to appease a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the breastbone
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The breastbone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it inclines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and shortness of breath, and immediately, and perhaps vomits blood, and the movement in the broken bone is apparent, and one feels it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and a cushion is placed between his shoulders, then press the shoulders, and bring together the ribs of the two ribs with your hands, and subtly put it equally in all ways that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put on plasters and tampons on top of a fine layer of salt, or other light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it over the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the bandage around the back, and tighten it properly, and check every hour the bandage, and if it loosens, then tighten it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to untie it, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and untie it, and remove the plaster, and address what has come there with methods of treatment;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then replace the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the fracture of the ribs only occurs in thick places near the back, and at the front, and they only break because they are slippery;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one feels it well on examination with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the fracture evenly, as is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage, if you need one.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the rib fracture is inclined inwards, the patient feels very great pain and pricking, like pleurisy, because the bone pierces the lung;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and breathes with difficulty, and often vomits a great quantity of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancients have applied great skill to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that one should administer foods that inflate the belly, to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, so that hot abscesses do not arise, if they have not already arisen.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have arisen, then we heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some say that one applies cupping glasses to the area, to strongly suck, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	however, there is doubt that the cupping glass might draw superfluities to the area due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to equally distribute the poultice around, then it should be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, with meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone that pierces the flesh, and the patient is in doubt, then it is necessary to cut into the area of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument underneath to protect the viscera;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone, and pull gently, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if a hot abscess appears, then apply cloths soaked in rose oil to the area;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area in the meantime as is necessary for an abscess, and let the patient lie often on the side where it is, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a fracture of the bones of the neck occurs, and it happens that it bends;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, observe if you see his hands softened and swollen and numb, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortal in several ways, and if he moves them and feels well when they are pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient will be cured, if care is taken.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, observe if the feet are softened, and if the symptoms are there which are in the hands, and on his back there is flatulence and involuntary evacuation;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when he is turned on his stomach, there is involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is turned onto his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that he is mortal.
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Therefore, do not labor in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, the matter is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that you observe if there is a hot abscess, then apply rose oil or egg yolk oil to it until it is calmed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that side where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone is separated, it is necessary to cut above the heart;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with flesh-generating ointment, until it is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", if you put your little finger of your left hand there, and set it even with the other side to your ability, then apply the plaster and the bandage on top, if you need it;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then pull it, and if there is a separated bone, cut above it and remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it happens, it is only a little lessening at the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and it breaks lengthwise, and slopes inwards, and the patient feels pain at the site, and throbbing, and the broken part swells.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, until you are on the fracture;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know what the fracture is and its form;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is only at the head, then set the fracture evenly, until it is in its natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, or it slopes inwards, then make the patient lie on his stomach, until the setting of that fracture is prepared for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it evenly, then apply the plaster, then apply a splint of wood or horn, and bind the fracture so that it does not move;
